[2026-03-14T00:57:49Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: Q.	Rayaprolu Subba Rao was a Telugu poet who wrote the poem I mentioned above. When X was speaking in Madras (now Chennai) during the run up to the British sending the Y to India without a single Indian member, Rayaprolu was tasked with translating the speech live into Telugu. Because most of the Tamil and Telugu people of Madras did not understand Hindi, it was common to engage local Tamil and Telugu scholars to translate speeches live. As X criticized the British exploitation of India sucking her dry, Rayaprolu composed a beautiful Telugu poem in strict meter on the spot, translating to: “India is like a nice milch cow. As Indians yelp like her calves, the cunning British are milking her dry with a grim determination.” ID X and Y. ‎<This message was edited>

[2026-03-14T04:45:42Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: 3.	X lived in Syracuse in modern Sicily, Italy in the 3rd century BCE. He invented a method of calculating the value of π by inscribing and circumscribing a circle with two polygons around it, each of up to 96 sides. Then he calculated the areas of the two polygons, and thereby obtained the result that π is between 223/71 and M/N. He is more famous for discovering the principle of Y and for building war machines to defend Syracuse from Roman invasion. You were taught M/N as a reasonable approximation for π in high school. ID X, Y, M, and N.

A small piece of bread or food and sometimes ale would be placed on the corpse or passed over it, and the outsider would eat or drink it while reciting a ritual. By consuming the food, the individual was believed to symbolically absorb the dead person’s moral burden, allowing the departed soul to enter the afterlife unburdened by sin.
